```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/workspace/script_context.py",
  "old_string": "def add_notice(notice: dict, notices: list) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Append (or, for order 'prepend'/'first', prepend) a notice dict to a notices list,\n    filling in the icon (from 'type'), plaintext 'text' (via html2text), and default order\n    when absent.  `notices` is a plain list -- the per-site `site_notices` list in the core\n    script, or `site_context['notices']`; passing the list (not site_context) lets this be\n    used before site_context is built and inside the notice-builder helpers.\n    \"\"\"\n    if 'message' not in notice:\n        console.print(f'[bold red]ERROR: Notice is missing the \"message\" key: {notice}')\n        sys.exit(1)\n    if 'icon' not in notice:\n        notice['icon'] = icon[notice['type']]\n    if 'text' not in notice:\n        notice['text'] = text_maker.handle(notice['message'])\n    order = notice['order'] if 'order' in notice else 'append'\n    if order == 'prepend' or order == 'first':\n        notices.insert(0, notice)\n    else:\n        notices.append(notice)\n\n\ndef add_notices(notices: list, site_notices: list) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Route each notice dict from a builder (wp_error/drush_error/check_*module) through\n    add_notice -- the canonical single path for adding notices to a site's notice list.\"\"\"\n    for notice in notices:\n        add_notice(notice, site_notices)",

notices/sections/attachments accumulate through the\n    per-site pipeline (including `check` hooks) and are consumed by the template render.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, site: dict):\n        super().__init__(site=site, notices=[], sections=[], attachments=[])\n\n    def add_notice(self, notice: dict) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Add a notice, filling in the icon (from 'type'), the plaintext 'text' (via html2text),\n        and honoring notice['order'] ('prepend'/'first' -> front of the list, else append).\n        \"\"\"\n        if 'message' not in notice:\n            console.print(f'[bold red]ERROR: Notice is missing the \"message\" key: {notice}')\n            sys.exit(1)\n        if 'icon' not in notice:\n            notice['icon'] = icon[notice['type']]\n        if 'text' not in notice:\n            notice['text'] = text_maker.handle(notice['message'])\n        order = notice['order'] if 'order' in notice else 'append'\n        if order == 'prepend' or order == 'first':\n            self['notices'].insert(0, notice)\n        else:\n            self['notices'].append(notice)\n\n    def add_notices(self, notices: list) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Add each notice dict returned by a builder (wp_error/drush_error/check_*module).\"\"\"\n        for notice in notices:\n            self.add_notice(notice)\n\n    def add_section(self, section: dict) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Add a report section (rendered into the email body).\"\"\"\n        self['sections'].append(section)\n\n    def add_attachment(self, attachment: dict) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Add an attachment (e.g. an inline image referenced by cid).\"\"\"\n        self['attachments'].append(attachment)"

## Assistant

Now the tokenize transform for the add-calls and bare `site_notices` reads:

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/tmp/claude-501/-workspace/b6bec5ef-fc02-458d-9b86-98132d9c168f/scratchpad/migrate_sitecontext.py",
  "content": "\"\"\"Convert sc.add_notice(<args>, site_notices) -> site_context.add_notice(<args>) (and\nadd_notices), and bare `site_notices` reads -> site_context['notices'].  Tokenize-based so\nstring/comment contents are never touched.\"\"\"\nimport io\nimport tokenize\n\nPATH = \"/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails\"\nsrc = open(PATH).read()\nlines = src.splitlines(keepends=True)\nline_off = [0]\nfor ln in lines:\n    line_off.append(line_off[-1] + len(ln))\n\ndef off(pos):\n    r, c = pos\n    return line_off[r - 1] + c\n\ntoks = list(tokenize.generate_tokens(io.StringIO(src).readline))\nsig = [t for t in toks if t.type not in (\n    tokenize.NL, tokenize.NEWLINE, tokenize.INDENT, tokenize.DEDENT,\n    tokenize.COMMENT, tokenize.ENCODING, tokenize.ENDMARKER)]\n\ndef match_close(start_i):\n    depth = 0\n    for j in range(start_i, len(sig)):\n        s = sig[j]\n        if s.type == tokenize.OP and s.string in \"([{\":\n            depth += 1\n        elif s.type == tokenize.OP and s.string in \")]}\":\n            depth -= 1\n            if depth == 0:\n                return j\n    raise RuntimeError(\"unbalanced\")\n\nedits = []\nn_add = n_read = 0\ni = 0\nwhile i < len(sig):\n    t = sig[i]\n    if (t.type == tokenize.NAME and t.string == \"sc\"\n            and i + 3 < len(sig) and sig[i+1].string == \".\"\n            and sig[i+2].string in (\"add_notice\", \"add_notices\")\n            and sig[i+3].string == \"(\"):\n        method = sig[i+2].string\n        open_i = i + 3\n        close_i = match_close(open_i)\n        assert sig[close_i-1].string == \"site_notices\" and sig[close_i-2].string == \",\", \\\n            f\"unexpected add-call shape near line {t.start[0]}\"\n        # sc.add_notice -> site_context.add_notice\n        edits.append((off(t.start), off(sig[i+2].end), f\"site_context.{method}\"))\n        # drop the trailing \", site_notices\" argument\n        edits.append((off(sig[close_i-2].start), off(sig[close_i-1].end), \"\"))\n        n_add += 1\n        i = close_i + 1\n        continue\n    if t.type == tokenize.NAME and t.string == \"site_notices\":\n        edits.append((off(t.start), off(t.end), \"site_context['notices']\"))\n        n_read += 1\n    i += 1\n\nedits.sort(key=lambda e: e[0], reverse=True)\nout = src\nfor s, e, r in edits:\n    out = out[:s] + r + out[e:]\nopen(PATH, \"w\").write(out)\nprint(f\"add-calls: {n_add}   bare-reads: {n_read}\")\n"
}
```

### ⚙ Tool call: `Edit`

```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/workspace/CLAUDE.md",
  "old_string": "- **Notices vs. news**: `sc.add_notice(notice, notices_list)` is the **canonical** way to add a\n  per-site notice — it takes the notice dict and the target list (the per-site `site_notices`\n  list, or `site_context['notices']`), filling in `icon`/`text`/`order` defaults; the builder\n  helpers route their lists through `sc.add_notices(list, site_notices)`. `add_news_item()` adds\n  an org-wide item to `sc.news` (config-inline `[News.<x>]` sub-tables + `*.toml` files in\n  `[News].folder` are both loaded by `load_news_items()`). Both take `type`\n  (`info`/`warning`/`alert` → emoji `icon`) and an HTML `message`; the plaintext `text` is\n  auto-generated via `html2text` if absent. Note existing notice dicts carry their own bespoke\n  `text`, so `add_notice`'s defaults are no-ops for them. New notices need a `csv` key\n  (`site,code,...`) — several report paths read `n[\"csv\"]`.",
  "new_string": "- **Notices vs. news**: `site_context` is a **`sc.SiteContext`** (a `dict` subclass, so\n  `site_context['notices'|'sections'|'attachments'|'site']` access is unchanged) constructed once\n  per processed site, as far up the per-site loop as possible (after the portal/not-requested/\n  Sandbox skips). Add to it via its methods — `site_context.add_notice(notice)` /\n  `.add_notices(list)` (builders: `wp_error`/`drush_error`/`check_*module`) / `.add_section(...)` /\n  `.add_attachment(...)` — this is the **canonical** path (the old module-level\n  `sc.add_notice`/`add_notices` free functions were removed). `add_notice` fills in\n  `icon` (from `type`), plaintext `text` (via `html2text`), and honors `order`\n  (`prepend`/`first` → front). `add_news_item()` (still an `sc` function) adds an org-wide item to\n  `sc.news` (config-inline `[News.<x>]` sub-tables + `*.toml` files in `[News].folder` are both\n  loaded by `load_news_items()`). Notice dicts carry their own bespoke `text`, so `add_notice`'s\n  defaults are no-ops for them; every notice needs a `csv` key (`site,code,...`) — several report\n  paths read `n[\"csv\"]`. Check hooks receive the `SiteContext` and call these methods directly\n  (see `check/umich/sitelens.py`); tests build one with `sc.SiteContext({\"name\": ...})`."
}

## Assistant

Done. The `SiteContext` refactor is complete and verified.

## What I did

Per your four decisions (dict subclass, delete the free functions, also add `add_section`/`add_attachment`, construct after the early skips):

1. **`script_context.py`** — replaced the module-level `add_notice`/`add_notices` free functions with `class SiteContext(dict)`. It keeps `site_context['notices'|'sections'|'attachments'|'site']` subscript access (so the ~20 read sites and the Jinja render are untouched) and owns four mutators: `add_notice`, `add_notices`, `add_section`, `add_attachment`.

2. **Core script** — `site_context = sc.SiteContext(site)` is now constructed **as far up as possible after the three early `continue`s** (portal / not-requested / Sandbox), replacing both the old `site_notices = []` and the later dict literal. A tokenize-based transform converted **47 add-calls** (`sc.add_notice(…, site_notices)` → `site_context.add_notice(…)`) and **6 bare `site_notices` reads** → `site_context['notices']`.

3. **`check/umich/sitelens.py`** — its `add_notice`, `add_attachment`, and `add_section` sites now use the methods.

4. **Tests** — `test_check_sitelens.py` and `test_dns.py` build `sc.SiteContext(...)` instead of plain dicts; added `tests/unit/test_site_context.py` (7 tests: construction, icon/text defaults, preserve-existing, missing-message exit, `order:first` prepend, bulk add, section/attachment).

5. **CLAUDE.md** — the notices section now documents the `SiteContext` API.

## Verification

- **Goldens byte-identical** — all 6 snapshots pass unchanged; this is the guarantee the behavior is preserved (the class methods do exactly what the free functions did, on the same list objects).
- `./run-tests` (all tiers incl. `live`) → **180 passed, 1 skipped** (the pre-existing SMTP skip).
- No orphaned `sc.add_notice`/`sc.add_notices` references remain; the program launches (`--help`).

## On your "better solution" ask

I pushed back on two points during the interview and you resolved them: the class is a `dict` subclass (not a full attribute rewrite, which would have churned ~20 extra access sites for no behavior gain), and the free functions are deleted rather than left as dual paths. The one remaining design smell I'd flag: `SiteContext` now mixes data (a dict of site fields) with behavior (the mutators) — a mild "god object." It's the right trade for this codebase given how pervasively `site_context['…']` is used, but if the per-site context grows more behavior later, extracting a dedicated `notices`/`sections` collection type would be the next step. Nothing to do now.

Nothing committed (per your convention).

## User

<command-message>code-review</command-message>
<command-name>/code-review</command-name>
<command-args>high</command-args>

## User

`high effort → 3+5 angles × 6 candidates → 1-vote verify (recall-biased) → ≤10 findings`

You are reviewing for **recall** at high effort: catch every real bug a careful
reviewer would catch in one sitting. At this level, catching real bugs matters
more than avoiding false positives. Err on the side of surfacing.

## Phase 0 — Gather the diff

Run `git diff @{upstream}...HEAD` (or `git diff main...HEAD` / `git diff HEAD~1`
if there's no upstream) to get the unified diff under review. If there are
uncommitted changes, or the range diff is empty, also run `git diff HEAD` and
include the working-tree changes in scope — the review often runs before the
commit. If a PR number, branch name, or file path was passed as an argument,
review that target instead. Treat this diff as the review scope.

## Phase 1 — Find candidates (3 correctness angles + 3 cleanup angles + 1 altitude angle + 1 conventions angle, up to 6 each)

Run **8 independent finder angles** via the Agent tool. Each
surfaces **up to 6 candidate findings** with `file`, `line`, a one-line
`summary`, and a concrete `failure_scenario`.

### Angle A — line-by-line diff scan

Read every hunk in the diff, line by line. Then Read the enclosing function for
each hunk — bugs in unchanged lines of a touched function are in scope (the PR
re-exposes or fails to fix them). For every line ask: what input, state, timing,
or platform makes this line wrong? Look for inverted/wrong conditions,
off-by-one, null/undefined deref, missing `await`, falsy-zero checks,
wrong-variable copy-paste, error swallowed in catch, unescaped regex metachars.

### Angle B — removed-behavior auditor

For every line the diff DELETES or replaces, name the invariant or behavior it
enforced, then search the new code for where that invariant is re-established.
If you can't find it, that's a candidate: a removed guard, a dropped error
path, a narrowed validation, a deleted test that was covering a real case.

### Angle C — cross-file tracer

For each function the diff changes, find its callers (Grep for the symbol) and
check whether the change breaks any call site: a new precondition, a changed
return shape, a new exception, a timing/ordering dependency. Also check callees:
does a parallel change in the same PR make a call unsafe?

### Reuse

The angles above hunt for bugs; this one and the next two hunt for cleanup in
the changed code. Flag new code that re-implements something the codebase
already has — Grep shared/utility modules and files adjacent to the change,
and name the existing helper to call instead.

### Simplification

Flag unnecessary complexity the diff adds: redundant or derivable state,
copy-paste with slight variation, deep nesting, dead code left behind. Name
the simpler form that does the same job.

### Efficiency

Flag wasted work the diff introduces: redundant computation or repeated I/O,
independent operations run sequentially, blocking work added to startup or
hot paths. Also flag long-lived objects built from closures or captured
environments — they keep the entire enclosing scope alive for the object's
lifetime (a memory leak when that scope holds large values); prefer a
class/struct that copies only the fields it needs. Name the cheaper
alternative.

### Altitude

Check that each change is implemented at the right depth, not as a fragile
bandaid. Special cases layered on shared infrastructure are a sign the fix
isn't deep enough — prefer generalizing the underlying mechanism over adding
special cases.

### Conventions (CLAUDE.md)

Find the CLAUDE.md files that govern the changed code: the user-level
~/.claude/CLAUDE.md, the repo-root CLAUDE.md, plus any CLAUDE.md or
CLAUDE.local.md in a directory that is an ancestor of a changed file (a
directory's CLAUDE.md only applies to files at or below it). Read each one
that exists, then check the diff for clear violations of the rules they state.

Only flag a violation when you can quote the exact rule and the exact line
that breaks it — no style preferences, no vague "spirit of the doc"
inferences. In the finding, name the CLAUDE.md path and quote the rule so the
report can cite it. If no CLAUDE.md applies, return nothing for this angle.

Cleanup, altitude, and conventions candidates use the same
`file`/`line`/`summary` shape; in `failure_scenario`, state the concrete
cost (what is duplicated, wasted, harder to maintain, or which CLAUDE.md rule
is broken) instead of a crash. Correctness bugs always outrank cleanup,
altitude, and conventions findings when the output cap forces a cut.

Pass every candidate with a nameable failure scenario through — finders that
silently drop half-believed candidates bypass the verify step and are the
dominant cause of misses.

## Phase 2 — Verify (1-vote, recall-biased)

Dedup near-duplicates (same defect, same location, same reason → keep one). For
each remaining candidate, run **one verifier** via the Agent tool:
give it the diff, the relevant file(s), and the candidate; it returns exactly
one of **CONFIRMED / PLAUSIBLE / REFUTED**.

**PLAUSIBLE by default** — do not refute a candidate for being "speculative" or
"depends on runtime state" when the state is realistic: concurrency races,
nil/undefined on a rare-but-reachable path (error handler, cold cache, missing
optional field), falsy-zero treated as missing, off-by-one on a boundary the
code does not exclude, retry storms / partial failures, regex/allowlist that
lost an anchor. These are PLAUSIBLE.

**REFUTED** only when constructible from the code: factually wrong (quote the
actual line); provably impossible (type/constant/invariant — show it); already
handled in this diff (cite the guard); or pure style with no observable effect.

Keep **CONFIRMED and PLAUSIBLE**. Drop REFUTED.

## Output

Return findings as a JSON array of at most 10 objects:

```json
[
  {
    "file": "path/to/file.ext",
    "line": 123,
    "summary": "one-sentence statement of the bug",
    "failure_scenario": "concrete inputs/state → wrong output/crash"
  }
]
```

Ranked most-severe first. If more than 10 survive, keep the 10 most
severe. If nothing survives verification, return `[]`.

## Code-quality review: uncommitted changes

### Finding 1 — Reuse (strong): four inline `[UMich].enabled` guards duplicate the new `umich_enabled()` verbatim
- **file**: `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`
- **line**: 1225-1228, 3574-3577, 3609-3612, 3695-3698 (helper defined at 1060-1072; only used at 1823 and 2152)
- **summary**: The diff introduces `umich_enabled()` but the four in-script guards still spell out the exact `"UMich" in sc.config and "enabled" in sc.config["UMich"] and sc.config["UMich"]["enabled"]` triplet by hand. Two of those blocks (3609-3612 and 3695-3698) are *newly added/rewritten in this same diff* (their new comments say "without the UMich guard ... crashed" / "Previously an unconditional `if True:`"), so they were written after the helper existed and should have called it.
- **failure_scenario**: Five copies of the same guard now exist (helper + 4 inline). If the enablement contract changes (e.g. `[UMich].enabled` becomes `[UMich].plugins.enabled`, or a truthiness/`is True` fix is needed), the helper gets fixed and the four inline copies silently diverge — exactly the class of latent non-UMich-path bug the change set is trying to retire. Replace each block with `if umich_enabled():` (and `if end_of_contract_year and umich_enabled():` at 3609).
  - Note: the two package guards at `check/umich/__init__.py:5` and `plugin/umich/__init__.py:5` are a separate case — they run at import time in other modules and can't cleanly import a main-script function, so leave those.

### Finding 2 — Reuse / duplication: `msgid_domain` lookup + default literal duplicated across files
- **file**: `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails` (line 3730) and `/workspace/check/umich/sitelens.py` (line ~207)
- **summary**: Both sites independently write `sc.config.get("Email", {}).get("msgid_domain", "webservices.umich.edu")`, repeating both the accessor chain and the magic default `"webservices.umich.edu"`.
- **failure_scenario**: The default institution domain is now hard-coded in two files. A deployment that changes the default (or a bug fix to the key name) must be made in both, and the sitelens copy is easy to miss because it lives in a plugin package. A one-line module-level helper (e.g. `def msgid_domain(): return sc.config.get("Email", {}).get("msgid_domain", "webservices.umich.edu")`) referenced from both removes the second literal. This is the "does the `sc.config.get("Email", {}).get(k, default)` pattern want a small helper" case called out in the brief.

### Finding 3 — Efficiency/simplification (minor): `[Email]` section fetched twice per site
- **file**: `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`
- **line**: 3730 (`sc.config.get("Email", {})` for `msgid_domain`) and 3809 (`email_cfg = sc.config.get("Email", {})`)
- **summary**: Inside the per-site loop the `[Email]` table is looked up twice per iteration instead of once.
- **failure_scenario**: Low cost (a dict `.get` on a small config), but it is redundant work every site and, more importantly, means the two consumers can drift. If Finding 2's helper is adopted, or `email_cfg` is hoisted above line 3730 and reused for `msgid_domain`, both the double-lookup and the duplication collapse into one source. Worth folding in only alongside Finding 2, not on its own.

### Things checked and cleared (no finding)
- `classify_hostname_dns` (lines 995-1055): no redundant work — it resolves A and AAAA once each, no repeated lookups; the `cloudflare_enabled`/empty-nets ternary at the call site is correct, not wasteful.

No orphaned variables/imports found from the refactor.

## Candidates

**1. `pantheon-sitehealth-emails:1414` (also the `month` call just below) — uncaught `TerminusError` inside the per-site loop**
- Summary: `get_old_metrics()` (line 526) calls `terminus_data("env:metrics", …)`, which now *raises* the new `TerminusError` on a fatal/undecodable result. Its call sites at ~1414/1420 (the `--import-older-metrics` path) are inside the per-site loop and are **not** wrapped in `try/except TerminusError`. The only catch in the whole file is at line 1202 (guarding the org-level `org:site:list`).
- Failure scenario: with `--import-older-metrics`, one site whose `env:metrics` call times out or returns non-JSON now aborts the entire run with an uncaught `TerminusError`, instead of skipping that site. This directly contradicts `terminus_data`'s own docstring ("inside the per-site loop, prefer checking fatal / `result is None` inline … so one bad site does not kill the whole run"). Confidence is medium: the pre-refactor code also crashed here (old `terminus()` returned `""` → `""["timeseries"]` → `TypeError`), so it's a pre-existing fragility the refactor renamed rather than a fresh regression — but the new named exception makes the intended per-site-skip contract easy to honor and it isn't.

---

**Finding 1 — [High confidence] P4 fix is incomplete: a transient DNS failure still produces a spurious "not behind Cloudflare" warning**
- **file:** `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`
- **line:** 1551 (classification) → notice emitted downstream at ~1674 via `fqdns_not_behind_cloudflare`
- **summary:** `classify_hostname_dns` returns counts `(0, 0)` on a transient resolver error, and the caller correctly guards the *not-in-DNS* branch with `and not dns_transient` (line 1544) — but the immediately following Cloudflare branch (`if cloudflare_enabled: if dns_points_at_cloudflare == 0 or dns_points_elsewhere != 0:`, lines 1550-1555) is **not** guarded by `dns_transient`, so a transient failure still appends the hostname to `fqdns_not_behind_cloudflare`.
- **failure_scenario:** A site with a custom domain and `[Cloudflare].enabled`, when the A/AAAA lookup hits `dns.resolver.Timeout` or `NoNameservers`: the owner receives BOTH the new "DNS lookup failed (transient) … re-run the report to retry" notice AND a contradictory "not behind Cloudflare" warning telling them to fix their Cloudflare configuration — exactly the misconfiguration-vs-transient confusion P4 set out to eliminate. The not-in-DNS path was fixed; the not-behind-Cloudflare path was missed.

---

**Finding 2 — [Medium confidence] P10's zero-traffic skip silently drops all accumulated alerts for a brand-new site**
- **file:** `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`
- **line:** 2817-2824 (`if not plan_on_day: … continue`)
- **summary:** When `plan_on_day` is empty (a site with no traffic rows in the query window), the loop `continue`s and no email is sent — discarding every notice already accumulated into `site_context` earlier in the iteration (frozen alert at 1293, paid-but-uninitialized-live-env alert at 1346, no-custom-domains alert at 1570, security-plugin alerts, etc.).
- **failure_scenario:** A newly created paid-plan site that is frozen (or has no custom domain) but has zero recorded traffic days: it accumulates a "site is frozen" / "no live environment but paid plan" alert, then hits `continue` at 2824 and the owner is never emailed. This is strictly better than the prior IndexError (which aborted the whole run), so it's not a regression against current behavior — but it's an incomplete fix: the intended outcome is presumably to still send the notice email, just without the chart/recommendation. The `continue` throws the alerts away.

---

No other defects found in the touched call sites: `terminus()`'s retry-on-expired-session is preserved for all callers (it's internal, and `terminus_data` wraps it); the `_errors, _fatal` discards at 2272/2418 are followed by `isinstance()` guards so a `None` result can't crash; the SMTP/`[Email]` config defaults reproduce the old literals byte-for-byte; and `build_plan_over_time`/`load_news_items` handle their empty/missing-`[News]` edge cases. `check/umich/sitelens.py`'s `add_notice`/`add_section`/`add_attachment` calls all resolve to the new `SiteContext` methods.</result>

## Assistant

Review complete — **5 findings** (high effort, 8 finder angles → dedup → verified), ranked most-severe first. The `SiteContext`/`terminus`/notice-migration mechanics all verified clean (Angle B confirmed byte-identical defaults and `SiteContext` logic; the goldens are the empirical proof). The findings are behavioral gaps, not mechanical breakage.

## Findings

1. **P4 incomplete — spurious "not behind Cloudflare" on transient DNS** (`pantheon-sitehealth-emails:1551`, correctness). I guarded the "not in DNS" branch with `not dns_transient` but not the following Cloudflare branch, so a resolver timeout emits both the "transient — re-run" notice *and* a contradictory "reconfigure Cloudflare" warning. This one is a genuine hole in my own P4 fix — found independently by two angles and verified against the code.

2. **Inconsistent per-site error policy** (`:1258`, `:1337`, `:530`, correctness). A transient Terminus failure at `plan:info`/`env:list` `sys.exit`s the whole run, and `get_old_metrics` raises an uncaught `TerminusError` — while sibling calls skip just the site. Contradicts `terminus_data`'s own "don't kill the whole run" docstring. Pre-existing abort behavior the diff touched but didn't align.

3. **P10 drops the whole email for a zero-traffic site** (`:2817`, correctness). The `continue` discards alerts already accumulated (frozen, not-in-DNS, plugin warnings). Better than the old `IndexError`, but the SPEC intent was to render a "no traffic yet" report, not send nothing.

4. **`umich_enabled()` not reused** (`:3609`, reuse). Four inline copies of the guard remain — two rewritten in this same diff after the helper existed.

5. **`msgid_domain` default duplicated** (`sitelens.py:207` + core `:3730`, reuse). Magic default `"webservices.umich.edu"` hard-coded in two files.

None of these break the passing test suite (they're on runtime paths the offline goldens stub out — transient DNS, live Terminus failures, zero-traffic-with-alerts). #1 is the one I'd fix before shipping; #2 and #3 are judgment calls about run-abort vs per-site-skip and whether a zero-traffic site should still get an alerts-only email.

Want me to fix any subset? I'd suggest at least **#1** (add `and not dns_transient` to the Cloudflare branch, with a matching DNS test), and I can do **#4/#5** as trivial cleanups. #2 and #3 change user-facing behavior, so I'd confirm the intended policy with you first.

## User

Fix all five findings.

## Assistant

All five fixes are in — **180 passed, 1 skipped** (incl. `live`), goldens byte-identical, program launches, and only the `umich_enabled()` helper body still contains the guard triplet.

## Fixes applied

**#1 — P4 Cloudflare/transient gap** (`:1550`). Guarded the Cloudflare classification with `if cloudflare_enabled and not dns_transient:`, so a transient DNS failure no longer emits a spurious "not behind Cloudflare" warning alongside the transient notice.

**#2 — Inconsistent per-site error policy.** A transient (`fatal`) failure now **skips the site** instead of aborting the whole run:
- `plan:info` and `env:list`: split the condition — `fatal`/`None` → `continue`; genuine structural data errors (missing SKU / no live env) still `sys.exit` ("should never happen").
- `get_old_metrics`: catches `TerminusError` and returns `[]` (older-metrics import is best-effort supplementary data — a bad site imports nothing rather than crashing the run).

**#3 — P10 dropped email** (`:2828`). Instead of `continue` (which discarded accumulated alerts and sent nothing), a zero-traffic site now seeds a synthetic plan-day at the report date, so it **renders the normal "not enough data yet" report with its alerts** — reusing the exact ≤4-month path the golden already exercises (one in-window month → `median_visitors` stays 0). Updated `test_zero_traffic_e2e` to assert the report now renders (`"months more data"` present) rather than being skipped.

**#4 — `umich_enabled()` reuse.** Replaced all four inline `[UMich].enabled` triplets in the core script with `umich_enabled()` (the two package `__init__` guards stay, as they can't import the main-script function).

**#5 — `msgid_domain()` helper.** Added `sc.msgid_domain()` to `script_context.py`; the core script and `sitelens.py` both call it, removing the duplicated default literal. This also collapsed the double `[Email]` lookup in the core render path.

## Test coverage notes

- **#3** is covered end-to-end (`test_zero_traffic_e2e` now renders).
- **#5** is exercised by every render (goldens + `test_eml_headers` assert the msgid domain).
- **#2**'s `get_old_metrics` best-effort path has a rewritten unit test (`test_get_old_metrics_returns_empty_on_failure_not_type_error`).
- **#1** and the `plan:info`/`env:list` `continue` branches are inline in `main()` on paths the offline harness stubs out (transient DNS, live Terminus failures), so they're verified by the classify-level test + goldens-show-no-regression + reasoning rather than a direct assertion — the same inline-in-`main()` limitation noted throughout this work. If you want, I can extract the per-hostname Cloudflare decision to make #1 directly unit-testable, but that's a larger refactor than the one-line fix warrants.

Nothing committed.

# Context Mode Stats

Show context savings for the current session.

## Instructions

1. Call the `mcp__context-mode__ctx_stats` MCP tool (no parameters needed).
2. **CRITICAL**: You MUST copy-paste the ENTIRE tool output as markdown text directly into your response message. Do NOT summarize, do NOT collapse, do NOT paraphrase. The user must see the full tables without pressing ctrl+o. Copy every line exactly as returned by the tool.
3. After the full output, add ONE sentence highlighting the key savings metric, e.g.:
   - "context-mode saved **12.4x** — 92% of data stayed in sandbox."
   - If no data yet: "No context-mode calls yet this session."

## Purge

- **`ctx_purge(confirm: true)`** — Permanently deletes all indexed content from the knowledge base. Use `/context-mode:ctx-purge` for this.

context-mode kept **97.9%** out of context this conversation — 14.5 MB / ~3.6M tokens' worth of file reads, agent runs, and tool output stayed in the sandbox, so only ~75.4K tokens reached the window.

One caveat worth flagging: that headline is context-mode's own model of what it *would have* cost, not a direct readout of this session — your `/context` panel shows the real window at 483K/1M tokens (48%), driven mostly by the Messages category (the finder/reviewer agent results and my edits, which flow through the conversation regardless). So the tool is genuinely saving a lot on raw file/output bytes, but don't read the "48× longer / 294 KB" figure as the actual current window size.

## User

<command-message>archive-session</command-message>
<command-name>/archive-session</command-name>

## User

Base directory for this skill: /workspace/.claude/skills/archive-session

# Archiving a development session

Run this at the end of a feature-development session, after the work is done but
**before committing**. It populates the feature's `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/`
folder with the record artifacts, then hands back to the user to commit.

Do the deterministic, secret-sensitive work (rendering, scrubbing, token math) via
`development/finalize-session.py` — never eyeball-redact a transcript yourself. This
skill's job is only to (a) figure out the target folder, (b) capture the two things
the script can't reach from outside a live session, and (c) run the script.

## Steps

1. **Determine the target folder.** It is `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` for the
   feature just built. If the user passed a slug as the argument, use
   `development/<that>/`. Otherwise infer it from the active `SPEC.md`, the git branch,
   or the feature under discussion; if it's ambiguous, ask the user. Create the folder
   if it doesn't exist. If prompts weren't saved yet, remind the user that
   `NN-*.prompt.md` files and any `design-notes/` are part of the record.

2. **Capture in-session-only data to gitignored `*.raw.txt` files** in the folder:
   - **rtk gain** — if `rtk` is on PATH, run `rtk gain` and save its stdout to
     `<dir>/rtk.raw.txt`. Skip if `rtk` is absent.
   - **context-mode /ctx-stats** — if context-mode is configured (the
     `mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_stats` tool is available), call it
     and save its output to `<dir>/ctx.raw.txt`. Skip if unavailable.
   - **/usage (dollar cost)** — you **cannot** invoke `/usage` yourself (it's a
     built-in CLI command, not a tool). Ask the user to run `/usage` and paste its
     output, then save that verbatim to `<dir>/usage.raw.txt`. This is the source of
     the cost figure — the script has no price table. If the user skips it, proceed;
     the cost section will just say it wasn't captured.

   Use `command -v rtk` to test for rtk. These `.raw.txt` files are gitignored; the
   script folds their contents into `statistics.md`.

3. **Run the script.** From the repo root:
   ```
   python development/finalize-session.py --dir development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug> \
       [--rtk-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/rtk.raw.txt] \
       [--ctx-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/ctx.raw.txt] \
       [--usage-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/usage.raw.txt] \
       [--label NN]
   ```
   It defaults to the newest session JSONL under `~/.claude/projects/-workspace/`.
   Pass `--label NN` only for a feature spanning multiple sessions (produces
   `transcript-NN.md` / `statistics-NN.md`). Omit the capture flags you didn't create.
   This writes `transcript.md` (scrubbed, committed), `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored),
   and `statistics.md` (committed).

4. **Scaffold `analytics.md`** in the folder if it doesn't already exist — a short
   template for the user's own narrative analysis (distinct from the auto-generated
   `statistics.md`, which is machine-written; do not hand-edit `statistics.md`):
   ```markdown
   # Analytics — <feature>

   _Your narrative: what went well, what to do differently, decisions worth remembering._
   ```

5. **Verify and report — do NOT commit.** Confirm `transcript.md` scrubbed cleanly
   with a **value-shaped** grep (matches actual secret VALUES, not prose mentions of
   the names — a session that merely discusses `SMTP_PASSWORD` etc. is fine):
   ```
   grep -nE '(SMTP_PASSWORD|AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID|AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL)[[:space:]]*[=:][[:space:]]*[^[:space:]«]|AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}|-----BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY-----|Bearer [A-Za-z0-9._-]{12,}' development/<dir>/transcript.md
   ```
   This should return nothing; any hit is a real secret value that slipped the regex —
   surface it, don't commit. (A bare quoted word that happens to look like a token is
   left alone by design.) List what was written. Then tell the user the folder is ready
   and that they can ask you to commit everything (code + `development/<dir>/`) in one
   commit, with you writing the commit message.
